<Rating>2< /Rating><Response>None<//Response>< Review>
Not So Good
I am a league bowler for more that 50 years. I would not recommend this house for league bowling. The PA system has been broke since we started 10 weeks ago. It sounds so bad that it is difficult to concentrate. The only speaker that works is on lane 29 and 30. It is so loud that it is just annoying. The oil machine does not seem to working properly. By the time that it reaches the of the lanes there is no oil on the lane.
They let kids bowl on lanes 31 and 32 are the are constantly running through the bowling area. The seating is not enough for a complete team of four to sit in the bowling area so congestion is very difficult. The back area where tables and chairs to exist are never clean so if you wish to sit there you must first bus your own table.
The management staff is friendly enough but unresponsive to our concerns. I do believe that a large part of the problem is directed from corporate higher ups. I will not return to this house.</Review>

<Rating>3< /Rating>< text>
I'm a new member.  When I purchased my membership an appointment with a trainer was setup to introduce me to the gym and to get a body composition assessment.  On the day that I visited with my trainer he was too busy talking about how he has clients that are losing 10-20 pounds weekly when following his plan.  Well as great as that sounds I've been on this planet long enough to know that this is not that healthy and is not good long term.  During our trip around the gym he took me into the class room and wanted to show me exercises I could do at home.  Well some exercises I couldn't do because I have arthritis.  This revelation through him off course so he was done showing me exercises and proceeded to take me back to the front to discuss how many sessions I should buy with him.  I told him I'd think about it.   2 weeks later my son has had the same visit with a trainer.   My son's trainer did a complete assessment which included a history of illnesses, pains or injury.  Asked about current ailments.  He then took my son around the gym and introduced him to the different machines.  He then told my son he'd like to train him but needed to get his mothers permission first.   I think the gym is great but the trainers are not consistent and they should be.  I don't care if you have a client losing 10-20 pounds a week and please don't tell me this to lure me in.  I've been back to exercise maybe a few times.  My son meets with his trainer 2x a week and loves it.  We've seen great progress and he's gone down 2 pants sizes.    I'd love to give more stars but I didn't have the greatest experience here.<//text>

< user_name>
Jake Nonnemaker<//user_name>
< date>
1578695568584<//date>
<rate>5<//rate>< text>
The Conejo Valley offers so much that one rarely has to leave.  But the area has a dearth of Persian restaurants. Luckily for us, we have Sadaf.

Their menu has so many diverse Persian dishes yet it's easy to navigate (tip: ask the friendly waiter for recommendations).  Tahdig, lentil soup, dolmeh, hummus, shirazi salad, polo dishes (flavored rice with chicken/lamb/beek), stwes and chicken/beef kabobs and koobidehs are all amazing.  There isn't anything on the menu that isn't 5-star quality and taste.

My favorite dish is the chicken koobideh.  It's seasoned ground chicken, cooked on a skewer on a charcoal grill.  It is amazingly juicy and delicious.

Service is fast and very friendly.  Don't let the white linens fool you: it's elegant but easy on the wallet. Lunch entrees are around $11. Dinners are $16+.<//text>

<name>James McPherson< /name>< time>
1502510961313< /time>
<Rate>5< /Rate>< review>
This isn't your average poke place. "Chirashi" is a Japanese word meaning scattered, and unlike other poke places that serve a bowl of rice and little portioned scoops of last night's salmon, Chirashi by Mr. 7 arranges your fresh slices of fish in a fanned out display. The way their food is served reflects the overall attitude of this place: attention to detail.

The ingredients in the bowls are presented in a way that highlights every individual piece of fish while still maintaining that cohesive poke bowl image. Each piece is carefully portioned out and strategically placed on top of a bed of sushi rice. Now, I don't think of myself as a sushi connoisseur, but I've had my fair share of fish, and I've grown accustomed to what I think is "good fish." And this place has GOOD FISH. The salmon is fresh, not too fishy, with a buttery texture. The Ahi Tuna is perfectly seared, lightly salted, and absolutely tender. Even the spicy tuna, which is usually regarded as a cheap filling for California rolls, is given the special treatment, with a subtle spicy flavor and an inexplicably creamy texture that appears to have little to no mayo used.

The sides are more understated, but are by no means underwhelming. The guacamole is insanely good (I doubled my portion) with a bright flavor and smooth texture that was pleasantly interrupted with diced red onion and tomato. This guacamole is very complimentary to the fresh flavors of the fish and doesn't feel out of place, unlike other poke places. The rest of the sides are well executed and taste fresh (crab meat, edamame, seaweed) but I really like that guacamole, if it wasn't clear.

Chirashi by Mr. 7 also looks INCREDIBLE. It's located across the street from Mt. San Antonio College, in a shopping center with affordable Asian restaurants and fast food places. But this place has extremely clean, refined decor featuring soft white LED bars and strips of pale birch wood that give the restaurant an extremely clean, modern aesthetic. Food should always be at the center of what makes a restaurant great, but the dining experience counts for something, and Chirashi by Mr. 7 hits the nail on the head by offering a unique environment that's trendy and cozy.

Google doesn't let me take off half a star, but my only grievance with this restaurant doesn't warrant the removal of a full star. That grievance is the price. It's pricey, which is an interesting move. College students are notoriously broke, and many of them (myself included) might walk in, see the price, and walk right back out. Let me explain why it's expensive, from my point of view. This isn't meant to be an affordable haven for starved, broke students who want a quick bite between classes. Chirashi by Mr. 7 is meant to be a dining experience, one that uses only the freshest and most flavorful ingredients, one that offers a premium eating environment, and one that doesn't leave you feeling like you blew the last of your paycheck on some rice in a bowl with raw fish on top.

If you're like me and you enjoy quality sushi, you MUST give this place a try. It's a decision that will turn a one time visit into a weekly ritual, and although your wallet won't be thanking you for it, your taste buds will.<//review>

< rating>
4< /rating>
< Text>
If you're looking for fresh raw fish to enjoy, look no further. I've been looking for a casual Japanese restaurant that serves fresh raw fish for a decent price and Mr.7 hit the spot. The chirashi was beautifully arranged and the fish was very fresh. The sushi rice was almost perfect - great authentic flavor, stickiness just right, cooked al dente, but the seasoning just a tad strong: cook with 20% less seasoning to make the rice flavor more subtle. I will choose this place over any poke place because cubed servings of fish does not taste anywhere as fulfilling and wholesome as sliced fish. That being said, my slices of fish were sliced thinner than the thinnest I've had in sushi joints - hence minus 1 star(would have been 2 stars if not for how perfect everything else was). If Mr.7 could slice 2mm thicker and charge a $1 more, I would rate this 5 star and it would honestly be my favorite restaurant. I forgot to mention that the spacious dining area and modern design is inviting and relaxing.</Text>

<Gmap_id>0x80c334c50bb741b7:0x67d017e386c3e1c1</Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
<time>1557671409990</time>< text>
My husband & I went here for a quick bite to eat. They have an extensive menu that was very sticky as if it had old oil on it. We both chose the $10.95 lunch salad. With it we got a chicken breast or pc of tilapia. Plus there were small pcs of small servings of carrot cake, cheesecake, caramel pecan brownies, & a tray of great looking cookies.

We normally split a Coke cause I only drink a few sips. They brought what looked to me 2be a liter of Coke much too large for both of us. This tasted awful; I thought it was diet and sent it back. The 2nd 1 arrived and was equally bad. The syrup/soda water mix had 2b off or diet was in the regular Cole spot.

The salad bar itself was fair. Nothing special, but u could make a decent salad off of it. I love cantelope and pineapple chunks, they had both; pineapple was excellent! The cantelope looked great, had good texture, but tasted musty; I didn't eat my 3 pcs.

Next came our chicken for me and fish for my husband. He'll eat anything, I am the picky one. 1st I smelled his fish fr across the table. Then when I looked at my chicken, all I saw was a cooked pc of meat, with grease floating on top. Both appeared to have been grilled, but both had this layer of grease on them. I put a napkin on the chicken to blot up this liquid. I wound up covering it up & passing to my husband, cause it looked so bad, the smell of both was nauseating me. He only picked at his fish. I dont think he had 1 bite. He decided we'd take boith home to our 2 doxies.

We split the 3 desserts. They were all only slivers, perfect size for a salad bar. I liked the cheesecake. He loved the carrot cake, his fav cake. The brownie looked great, but that's all. It tasted as if it were missing something. Oh and the beautiful spread of cookies...not so  good either.

We pd & left, carrying our box of chicken & fish for our dogs. We drove to a shop in the same strip mall, went in a few minutes. When we returned & he opened my car door, I told him he had to put the chicken & fish in the trunk. The aroma was so over-powering, that my stomach turned, again. Instead, he picked the box up and threw it in a nearby trashcan, adding that he was bothered by the smell & it not being fit to feed our dogs.

I gave it 2 stars for the carrot cake & cheesecake slivers. They were just the right size for a taste. Plus they were good. Given the lacking brownie, I'd guess they weren't made in house.</text>
